Was looking at the specs on the OneXPlayer ,gpd win 3 and noticed that they use the Iris Xe 96EU ver, it's total FP32 perf was rated at 2.46 Teraflops. The RDNA2 chip in the Steam Deck maxes out at around 1.6 Teraflops (FP32)  That breaks down to 512cores on the RDNA2 chip vs 768cores on the Intel  The Tiger Lake CPU clocks higher (3ghz base, boosts to 4.8ghz, all core 4.3ghz) vs 2.4ghz base / all core boost to 3.5ghz on the AMD chip  Teraflops aren't the end all of performance metrics in games, but it does play a major a factor in many of them. The Steam Deck is the slowest handheld PC when it launches after all. this shouldn't surprise anyone for its value.

To claim that all three options include SSDs isn't really correct. While two of them do include NVMe SSDs, eMMC storage isn't usually referred to as an "SSD." However, as long as the eMMC storage loads games as fast as traditional SATA SSDs, the game-load times should be virtually identical across all three models, as NVMe SSDs load games virtually (if not literally) no faster than SATA SSDs. It's silly how many people don't know this and act like their overpriced Samsung NVMe SSD is special.

To all the people who say this is the 'switch killer', you need to understand that there's a clear market for the Nintendo switch which is completely outside of who will buy this handheld. I'm not underplaying the great work from valve here, but Nintendo is a household name whereas Valve unfortunately not, so a product like this might be intimidating to alot of potential buyers. Furthermore, this is most definitely a niche product, unlike the switch, this handheld is not releasing for Valve to release their own games on, but for people to play preexisting PC games in handheld mode. Another point to make is that this isn't really a handheld like the switch is. Not in the same right, it estimates 2-8 hours battery which essentially means most graphically intensive games will be about 3 hours playtime, it's significantly larger, and also the button layout is very much again, intimidating. And finally, historically Valve is just simply unable to compete with the major video game companies with their hardware. For example, the PSVR, a perriferal for the PS4 sold over 5 million units whereas the valve index is estimated to have sold about a tenth of that. I'm sure there's someone typing out an elongated reply about how I'm a 'nintendrone' and how I'm sucking up to a billion dollar company, but this really isn't competition for the switch, you need to understand that.
